   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">
    Research Triangle
   </h1>
   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
    <div class="noprint" id="siteSub">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div>

       <a href="/wiki/Research_Triangle_Park" title="Research Triangle Park">
        Research Triangle Park
       </a>
       . For the adjacent geographic area, see
       <a href="/wiki/Piedmont_Triad" title="Piedmont Triad">
        Piedmont Triad
       </a>

      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <b>
        Research Triangle
       </b>
       , commonly referred to as simply
       <b>
        The Triangle
       </b>
       , is a region in the
       <a href="/wiki/Piedmont_(United_States)" title="Piedmont (United States)">
        Piedmont
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">
        North Carolina
       </a>
       in the United States, anchored by
       <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_State_University" title="North Carolina State University">
        North Carolina State University
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Duke_University" title="Duke University">
        Duke University
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_North_Carolina_at_Chapel_Hill" title="University of North Carolina at Chapel Hill">
        University of North Carolina at Chapel Hill
       </a>
       , and the cities of
       <a href="/wiki/Raleigh,_North_Carolina" title="Raleigh, North Carolina">
        Raleigh
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Durham,_North_Carolina" title="Durham, North Carolina">
        Durham
       </a>
       and the town of
       <a href="/wiki/Chapel_Hill,_North_Carolina" title="Chapel Hill, North Carolina">
        Chapel Hill
       </a>
       . The eight-county region, officially named the
       <b>
        Raleigh–Durham–Chapel Hill
       </b>
       <a href="/wiki/Combined_statistical_area" title="Combined statistical area">
        combined statistical area
       </a>
       (CSA), comprises the Raleigh and Durham–Chapel Hill metropolitan areas and the Dunn, Henderson, Oxford, and Sanford Micropolitan Statistical Areas. A 2013 Census estimate put the population at 2,037,430, making it the second largest metropolitan area in the state of North Carolina behind
       <a href="/wiki/Charlotte_metropolitan_area" title="Charlotte metropolitan area">
        Charlotte
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Raleigh-Durham_television_station_history" title="Raleigh-Durham television station history">
        Raleigh–Durham television market
       </a>
       includes a broader 24-county area which includes Fayetteville, and has a population of 2,726,000 persons.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The "Triangle" name was cemented in the public consciousness in the 1950s with the creation of
       <a href="/wiki/Research_Triangle_Park" title="Research Triangle Park">
        Research Triangle Park
       </a>
       , home to numerous high-tech companies and enterprises. Although the name is now used to refer to the geographic region, "the Triangle" originally referred to the universities, whose research facilities, and the educated workforce they provide, have historically served as a major attraction for businesses located in the region. The region should not be confused with
       <a href="/wiki/Piedmont_Triad" title="Piedmont Triad">
        The Triad
       </a>
       , which is a North Carolina region adjacent to and directly west of the Triangle comprising
       <a href="/wiki/Greensboro,_North_Carolina" title="Greensboro, North Carolina">
        Greensboro
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Winston-Salem,_North_Carolina" title="Winston-Salem, North Carolina">
        Winston-Salem
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/High_Point,_North_Carolina" title="High Point, North Carolina">
        High Point
       </a>
       , among other cities.
      </p>
      <p>
       Most of the Triangle is part of North Carolina's
       <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina%27s_2nd_congressional_district" title="North Carolina's 2nd congressional district">
        second
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina%27s_4th_congressional_district" title="North Carolina's 4th congressional district">
        fourth
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina%27s_13th_congressional_district" title="North Carolina's 13th congressional district">
        thirteenth
       </a>
       congressional districts.
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Counties">
        Counties
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Research_Triangle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Counties">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Research-Triangle_2014.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="266" data-file-width="654" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Research-Triangle_2014.png/400px-Research-Triangle_2014.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Research-Triangle_2014.png/600px-Research-Triangle_2014.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/ad/Research-Triangle_2014.png 2x" width="400"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Research-Triangle_2014.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Counties contained in the Research Triangle.
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #008000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          Three core counties: Wake, Durham, Orange
         </div>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #8A2BE2; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          Additional counties included in Raleigh–Durham–Cary-Chapel Hill Combined Statistical Area, per the U.S. Census Bureau
         </div>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #808080; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          Other counties sometimes included in the Research Triangle descriptions
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Depending on which definition of the Research Triangle region is used, as few as three or as many as 16 counties are included as part of the region. All of these counties when included hold a population over 2,167,000 people.
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Chatham_County,_North_Carolina" title="Chatham County, North Carolina">
         Chatham
        </a>
        ‡¶
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Durham_County,_North_Carolina" title="Durham County, North Carolina">
         Durham
        </a>
        *‡¶
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Edgecombe_County,_North_Carolina" title="Edgecombe County, North Carolina">
         Edgecombe
        </a>
        ¶
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Franklin_County,_North_Carolina" title="Franklin County, North Carolina">
         Franklin
        </a>
        ‡¶
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Granville_County,_North_Carolina" title="Granville County, North Carolina">
         Granville
        </a>
        ‡¶
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Harnett_County,_North_Carolina" title="Harnett County, North Carolina">
         Harnett
        </a>
        ‡¶
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Johnston_County,_North_Carolina" title="Johnston County, North Carolina">
         Johnston
        </a>
        ‡¶
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Lee_County,_North_Carolina" title="Lee County, North Carolina">
         Lee
        </a>
        ‡¶
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Moore_County,_North_Carolina" title="Moore County, North Carolina">
         Moore
        </a>
        ¶
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Nash_County,_North_Carolina" title="Nash County, North Carolina">
         Nash
        </a>
        ‡¶
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Orange_County,_North_Carolina" title="Orange County, North Carolina">
         Orange
        </a>
        *‡¶
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Person_County,_North_Carolina" title="Person County, North Carolina">
         Person
        </a>
        ‡¶
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Vance_County,_North_Carolina" title="Vance County, North Carolina">
         Vance
        </a>
        ‡¶
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Wake_County,_North_Carolina" title="Wake County, North Carolina">
         Wake
        </a>
        *‡¶
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Warren_County,_North_Carolina" title="Warren County, North Carolina">
         Warren
        </a>
        ¶
       </li>
      </ul>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        * – Most restrictive definition, comprising the three core counties of Wake, Durham and Orange
       </dd>
       <dd>
        ‡ – U.S. Census Bureau definition, taken from the counties included in the Raleigh–Durham–Cary–Chapel Hill Combined Statistical Area
       </dd>
       <dd>
        ¶ – Most liberal definition of the Research Triangle region, as defined by the Research Triangle Regional Partnership
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RTRP_3-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-RTRP-3">
          [3]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       Raleigh–Durham–Cary-Chapel Hill Combined Statistical Area Population (Census Estimates 2015) 2,211,022
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Cities">
        Cities
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Research_Triangle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Cities">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Downtown-Raleigh-from-Western-Boulevard-Overpass-20081012.jpeg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" height="186" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Downtown-Raleigh-from-Western-Boulevard-Overpass-20081012.jpeg/280px-Downtown-Raleigh-from-Western-Boulevard-Overpass-20081012.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Downtown-Raleigh-from-Western-Boulevard-Overpass-20081012.jpeg/420px-Downtown-Raleigh-from-Western-Boulevard-Overpass-20081012.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Downtown-Raleigh-from-Western-Boulevard-Overpass-20081012.jpeg/560px-Downtown-Raleigh-from-Western-Boulevard-Overpass-20081012.jpeg 2x" width="280"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Downtown-Raleigh-from-Western-Boulevard-Overpass-20081012.jpeg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Raleigh,_North_Carolina" title="Raleigh, North Carolina">
          Raleigh
         </a>
         , the capital of North Carolina.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Downtown_Durham.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2265" data-file-width="3844" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Downtown_Durham.jpg/280px-Downtown_Durham.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Downtown_Durham.jpg/420px-Downtown_Durham.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Downtown_Durham.jpg/560px-Downtown_Durham.jpg 2x" width="280"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Downtown_Durham.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Downtown Durham, North Carolina.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Triangle region, as defined for statistical purposes as the
       <b>
        Raleigh–Durham–Chapel Hill CSA
       </b>
       , comprises eight counties, although the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Census_Bureau" title="U.S. Census Bureau">
        U.S. Census Bureau
       </a>
       divided the region into two metropolitan statistical areas and one micropolitan area in 2003. The Raleigh metropolitan area comprises Wake, Nash, Franklin, and Johnston Counties; the Durham-Chapel Hill metropolitan area comprises Durham, Orange, Chatham, and Person Counties; and the Dunn micropolitan area comprises Harnett County. Some area television stations define the region as
       <b>
        Raleigh–Durham–Fayetteville
       </b>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Fayetteville,_North_Carolina" title="Fayetteville, North Carolina">
        Fayetteville, North Carolina
       </a>
       , is over 50 miles (80 km) from Raleigh, but is part of the Triangle television
       <a href="/wiki/Media_market" title="Media market">
        market
       </a>
       .
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Education">
        Education
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Research_Triangle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Education">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Public secondary education in the Triangle is similar to that of the majority of the state of North Carolina, in which there are county-wide school systems (the exception is
       <a href="/wiki/Chapel_Hill-Carrboro_City_Schools" title="Chapel Hill-Carrboro City Schools">
        Chapel Hill-Carrboro City Schools
       </a>
       within Orange County but apart from Orange County Schools). Based in Cary, the
       <a href="/wiki/Wake_County_Public_School_System" title="Wake County Public School System">
        Wake County Public School System
       </a>
       , which includes the cities of Raleigh and Cary, is the largest school system in the state of North Carolina and the 15th-largest in the United States, with average daily entollment of 159,949 as of the second month of the 2016-17 school year.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Other larger systems in the region include Durham Public Schools (about 33,000 students) and rapidly growing Johnston County Schools (about 31,000 students).
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Institutions_of_higher_education">

         ]

      </h3>

       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:446px;max-width:446px">
        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:162px;max-width:162px">

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">
        Sports
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Research_Triangle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Sports">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="College_sports">
        College sports
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Research_Triangle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: College sports">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Duke-Carolina_basketball_tip-off_2006.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="523" data-file-width="788" height="186" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Duke-Carolina_basketball_tip-off_2006.jpg/280px-Duke-Carolina_basketball_tip-off_2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Duke-Carolina_basketball_tip-off_2006.jpg/420px-Duke-Carolina_basketball_tip-off_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Duke-Carolina_basketball_tip-off_2006.jpg/560px-Duke-Carolina_basketball_tip-off_2006.jpg 2x" width="280"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Duke-Carolina_basketball_tip-off_2006.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Tip-off of a Duke-UNC basketball game at the
         <a href="/wiki/Dean_Smith_Center" title="Dean Smith Center">
          Dean Smith Center
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       With the significant number of universities and colleges in the area and the relative absence of major league professional sports,
       <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">
        NCAA
       </a>
       sports are very popular, particularly those sports in which the
       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Coast_Conference" title="Atlantic Coast Conference">
        Atlantic Coast Conference
       </a>
       participates, most notably basketball.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Duke_Blue_Devils" title="Duke Blue Devils">
        Duke Blue Devils
       </a>
       (representing
       <a href="/wiki/Duke_University" title="Duke University">
        Duke University
       </a>
       in Durham),
       <a href="/wiki/NC_State_Wolfpack" title="NC State Wolfpack">
        NC State Wolfpack
       </a>
       (representing
       <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_State_University" title="North Carolina State University">
        North Carolina State University
       </a>
       in Raleigh), and
       <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Tar_Heels" title="North Carolina Tar Heels">
        North Carolina Tar Heels
       </a>
       (representing the
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_North_Carolina_at_Chapel_Hill" title="University of North Carolina at Chapel Hill">
        University of North Carolina at Chapel Hill
       </a>
       ) are all members of the
       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Coast_Conference" title="Atlantic Coast Conference">
        ACC
       </a>
       . Rivalries among these schools are very strong, fueled by proximity to each other, with annual competitions in every sport. Adding to the rivalries is the large number of graduates the high schools in the region send to each of the local universities. It is very common for students at one university to know many students attending the other local universities, which increases the opportunities for "bragging" among the schools. The four ACC schools in the state, Duke, North Carolina, North Carolina State, and
       <a href="/wiki/Wake_Forest_University" title="Wake Forest University">
        Wake Forest University
       </a>
       (the last of which was originally located in the town of Wake Forest before moving to Winston-Salem in 1956), are referred to as
       <a href="/wiki/Tobacco_Road" title="Tobacco Road">
        Tobacco Road
       </a>
       by sportscasters, particularly in basketball. All four teams consistently produce high-caliber teams. Each of the Triangle-based universities listed has won at least two NCAA Basketball national championships.
      </p>
      <p>
       Three
       <a href="/wiki/Historically_black_colleges_and_universities" title="Historically black colleges and universities">
        historically black colleges
       </a>
       , including recent Division I arrival
       <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Central_University" title="North Carolina Central University">
        North Carolina Central University
       </a>
       and Division II members
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Augustine%27s_College_(North_Carolina)" title="St. Augustine's College (North Carolina)">
        St. Augustine College
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Shaw_University" title="Shaw University">
        Shaw University
       </a>
       also boost the popularity of college sports in the region.
      </p>
      <p>
       Other colleges in the Triangle that field intercollegiate teams include
       <a href="/wiki/Campbell_University" title="Campbell University">
        Campbell University
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Meredith_College" title="Meredith College">
        Meredith College
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/William_Peace_University" title="William Peace University">
        William Peace University
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Professional_sports">
        Professional sports
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Research_Triangle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Professional sports">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RBC_Center_Stanley_Cup_Championship.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1712" data-file-width="2288" height="195" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/RBC_Center_Stanley_Cup_Championship.jpg/260px-RBC_Center_Stanley_Cup_Championship.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/RBC_Center_Stanley_Cup_Championship.jpg/390px-RBC_Center_Stanley_Cup_Championship.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/RBC_Center_Stanley_Cup_Championship.jpg/520px-RBC_Center_Stanley_Cup_Championship.jpg 2x" width="260"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RBC_Center_Stanley_Cup_Championship.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         2006 Stanley Cup ceremony at the RBC Center (now
         <a href="/wiki/PNC_Arena" title="PNC Arena">
          PNC Arena
         </a>
         )
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The region has only one professional team of the
       <a href="/wiki/Major_professional_sports_leagues_in_the_United_States_and_Canada" title="Major professional sports leagues in the United States and Canada">
        four major sports
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Carolina_Hurricanes" title="Carolina Hurricanes">
        Carolina Hurricanes
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">
        NHL
       </a>
       , based in Raleigh. Since moving to the Research Triangle region from
       <a href="/wiki/Hartford,_Connecticut" title="Hartford, Connecticut">
        Hartford, Connecticut
       </a>
       , they have enjoyed great success, including winning a
       <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Cup" title="Stanley Cup">
        Stanley Cup
       </a>
       . With only one top-level professional sports option, minor league sports are quite popular in the region. The
       <a href="/wiki/Durham_Bulls" title="Durham Bulls">
        Durham Bulls
       </a>
       in downtown Durham are a AAA Minor League baseball affiliate of the
       <a href="/wiki/Tampa_Bay_Rays" title="Tampa Bay Rays">
        Tampa Bay Rays
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/Carolina_Mudcats" title="Carolina Mudcats">
        Carolina Mudcats
       </a>
       , based in Zebulon, 10 miles east of Raleigh, are the Advanced-A affiliate of the
       <a href="/wiki/Milwaukee_Brewers" title="Milwaukee Brewers">
        Milwaukee Brewers
       </a>
       . In Cary,
       <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_FC" title="North Carolina FC">
        North Carolina FC
       </a>
       plays in the second-level
       <a href="/wiki/United_Soccer_League" title="United Soccer League">
        United Soccer League
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Courage" title="North Carolina Courage">
        North Carolina Courage
       </a>
       began play in the
       <a href="/wiki/National_Women%27s_Soccer_League" title="National Women's Soccer League">
        National Women's Soccer League
       </a>
       in 2017 after the owner of North Carolina FC bought the NWSL franchise rights of the
       <a href="/wiki/Western_New_York_Flash" title="Western New York Flash">
        Western New York Flash
       </a>
       and relocated the NWSL franchise to the Triangle.
      </p>

         </a>
        </td>
       </tr>

      <p>
       The area also had a team in the fledgling
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_League_of_American_Football" title="World League of American Football">
        World League of American Football
       </a>
       – however, the
       <a href="/wiki/Raleigh%E2%80%93Durham_Skyhawks" title="Raleigh–Durham Skyhawks">
        Raleigh–Durham Skyhawks
       </a>
       , coached by
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Gabriel" title="Roman Gabriel">
        Roman Gabriel
       </a>
       , did not exactly cover themselves in glory; they lost all 10 games of their inaugural (and only) season in 1991. The team folded after that, being replaced in the league by the
       <a href="/wiki/Ohio_Glory" title="Ohio Glory">
        Ohio Glory
       </a>
       , which fared little better at 1-9, ultimately suffering the same fate – along with the other six teams based in North America – when the league took a two-year hiatus, returning as a six-team all-European league in 1995.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Badminton">
        Badminton
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Research_Triangle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Badminton">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       With over 1200 active participants in multiple recreation centers and university campuses throughout the area, Research Triangle is home to one of the largest badminton communities in the Southeastern United States. The American Badminton Academy is also located here in a dedicated facility with seven permanent courts. The Academy is unique among U.S. badminton facilities in that it hosts an international player development program run by Dennis Christensen, an Olympic-level coach from Denmark.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Commerce">
        Commerce
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Research_Triangle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Commerce">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Anchored by leading technology firms, government and world-class universities, medical centers and schools, the area's economy has performed exceptionally well. Significant increases in employment, earnings, personal income, and retail sales are projected over the next 15 years.
      </p>
      <p>
       The region's growing high-technology community includes such companies as
       <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">
        IBM
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/SAS_Institute" title="SAS Institute">
        SAS Institute
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cisco_Systems" title="Cisco Systems">
        Cisco Systems
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/NetApp" title="NetApp">
        NetApp
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Red_Hat" title="Red Hat">
        Red Hat
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EMC_Corporation" title="EMC Corporation">
        EMC Corporation
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Credit_Suisse_First_Boston" title="Credit Suisse First Boston">
        Credit Suisse First Boston
       </a>
       . In addition to high-tech, the region is consistently ranked in the top three in the U.S. with concentration in life science companies. Some of these companies include
       <a href="/wiki/GlaxoSmithKline" title="GlaxoSmithKline">
        GlaxoSmithKline
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biogen_Idec" title="Biogen Idec">
        Biogen Idec
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/BASF" title="BASF">
        BASF
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Merck_%26_Co." title="Merck &amp; Co.">
        Merck &amp; Co.
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Novo_Nordisk" title="Novo Nordisk">
        Novo Nordisk
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Novozymes" title="Novozymes">
        Novozymes
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Pfizer" title="Pfizer">
        Pfizer
       </a>
       . Research Triangle Park and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Centennial_Campus" title="Centennial Campus">
        North Carolina State University's Centennial Campus
       </a>
       in Raleigh support innovation through R&amp;D and technology transfer among the region's companies and research universities (including Duke University and the University of North Carolina at Chapel Hill).
      </p>
      <p>
       The area has fared relatively well during the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Late-2000s_recession" title="Late-2000s recession">
        late-2000s recession
       </a>
       , ranked as the strongest region in North Carolina by the
       <a href="/wiki/Brookings_Institution" title="Brookings Institution">
        Brookings Institution
       </a>
       and among the top 40 in the country. The change in unemployment during 2008 to 2009 was 4.6% and home prices was 2%. The
       <a href="/wiki/Greensboro,_North_Carolina" title="Greensboro, North Carolina">
        Greensboro
       </a>
       metropolitan area was listed among the second-weakest and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charlotte" title="Charlotte">
        Charlotte
       </a>
       area among the middle in the country.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">
        Transportation
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Research_Triangle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Transportation">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Freeways_and_primary_designated_routes">
        Freeways and primary designated routes
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Research_Triangle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Freeways and primary designated routes">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2008-07-25_I-85_from_Davis_Dr_in_RTP.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/2008-07-25_I-85_from_Davis_Dr_in_RTP.jpg/180px-2008-07-25_I-85_from_Davis_Dr_in_RTP.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/2008-07-25_I-85_from_Davis_Dr_in_RTP.jpg/270px-2008-07-25_I-85_from_Davis_Dr_in_RTP.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/2008-07-25_I-85_from_Davis_Dr_in_RTP.jpg/360px-2008-07-25_I-85_from_Davis_Dr_in_RTP.jpg 2x" width="180"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2008-07-25_I-85_from_Davis_Dr_in_RTP.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         I-40
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2008-07-23_Morning_Durham_from_Fayetteville_St_over_NC_147.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/2008-07-23_Morning_Durham_from_Fayetteville_St_over_NC_147.jpg/180px-2008-07-23_Morning_Durham_from_Fayetteville_St_over_NC_147.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/2008-07-23_Morning_Durham_from_Fayetteville_St_over_NC_147.jpg/270px-2008-07-23_Morning_Durham_from_Fayetteville_St_over_NC_147.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/2008-07-23_Morning_Durham_from_Fayetteville_St_over_NC_147.jpg/360px-2008-07-23_Morning_Durham_from_Fayetteville_St_over_NC_147.jpg 2x" width="180"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2008-07-23_Morning_Durham_from_Fayetteville_St_over_NC_147.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The Durham Freeway
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Triangle proper is served by two major
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstate_highway" title="Interstate highway">
        interstate highways
       </a>
       :
       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_40" title="Interstate 40">
        I-40
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_85" title="Interstate 85">
        I-85
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_87_(North_Carolina)" title="Interstate 87 (North Carolina)">
        I-87
       </a>
       along with their
       <a href="/wiki/Spur_route" title="Spur route">
        spurs
       </a>
       :
       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_440_(North_Carolina)" title="Interstate 440 (North Carolina)">
        I-440
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstate_540_(North_Carolina)" title="Interstate 540 (North Carolina)">
        I-540
       </a>
       , and seven
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Numbered_Highways" title="United States Numbered Highways">
        U.S. Routes
       </a>
       :
       <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_1_in_North_Carolina" title="U.S. Route 1 in North Carolina">
        1
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_15" title="U.S. Route 15">
        15
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_64" title="U.S. Route 64">
        64
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_70_in_North_Carolina" title="U.S. Route 70 in North Carolina">
        70
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_264" title="U.S. Route 264">
        264
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_401" title="U.S. Route 401">
        401
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_501" title="U.S. Route 501">
        501
       </a>
       . US Highways 15 and 501 are multiplexed through much of the region as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Route_15/501_in_North_Carolina" title="U.S. Route 15/501 in North Carolina">
        US 15-501
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_95" title="Interstate 95">
        I-95
       </a>
       passes 30 miles east of Raleigh through Johnston County, with a spur route,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstate_495_(North_Carolina)" title="Interstate 495 (North Carolina)">
        I-495
       </a>
       , connecting I-95 at Rocky Mount, NC to Raleigh via the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Knightdale_Bypass" title="Knightdale Bypass">
        US 64-264 Bypass
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The two interstates diverge from one another in Orange County, with I-85 heading northeast through northern Durham County toward
       <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">
        Virginia
       </a>
       , while
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/I-40" title="I-40">
        I-40
       </a>
       travels southeast through southern Durham, through the center of the region, and serves as the primary freeway through Raleigh. The related loop freeways I-440 and I-540 are primarily located in Wake County around Raleigh. I-440 begins at the interchange of US 1 and I-40 southwest of downtown Raleigh and arcs as a multiplex with US 1 northward around downtown with the formal designation as the Cliff Benson/Raleigh Beltline (cosigned with US 1 on three-fourths of its northern route) and ends at its junction with I-40 in southeast Raleigh. I-540, sometimes known as the Raleigh Outer Loop, extends from the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Knightdale_Bypass" title="Knightdale Bypass">
        US 64-264 Bypass
       </a>
       to I-40 just inside Durham County, where it continues across the interstate as a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_route" title="State route">
        state route
       </a>
       (NC 540), prior to its becoming a
       <a href="/wiki/Toll_road" title="Toll road">
        toll road
       </a>
       from the NC 54 interchange to the current terminus at NC Highway 55 near Holly Springs. I-95 serves the extreme eastern edge of the region, crossing north-south through suburban Johnston County.
      </p>
      <p>
       U.S. Routes 1, 15, and 64 primarily serve the region as limited-access freeways or multilane highways with
       <a href="/wiki/Frontage_road" title="Frontage road">
        access roads
       </a>
       . US 1 enters the region from the southwest as the Claude E. Pope Memorial Highway and travels through suburban Apex where it merges with US 64 and continues northeast through Cary. The two highways are codesignated for about 2 miles (3.2 km) until US 1 joins I-440 and US 64 with I-40 along the Raleigh–Cary border. Capital Boulevard, which is designated US 1 for half of its route and US 401 the other is not a limited-access freeway, although it is a major thoroughfare through northeast Raleigh and into the northern downtown area.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Highway_147" title="North Carolina Highway 147">
        North Carolina Highway 147
       </a>
       is a limited-access freeway that connects I-85 with Toll Route NC 540 in northwestern Wake County. The older, toll-free portion of the four-lane route—known as the Durham Freeway or the I.L. "Buck" Dean Expressway—traverses downtown Durham and extends through Research Triangle Park to I-40. The Durham Freeway is often used as a detour or alternate route for I-40 through southwestern Durham the Chapel Hill area in cases of traffic accident, congestion or road construction delays. The tolled portion of NC 147, called the Triangle Expressway—North Carolina's first modern toll road when it opened to traffic in late 2011—continues past I-40 to Toll NC 540. Both Toll NC 147 and Toll NC 540 are modern facilities which collect tolls using transponders and license plate photo-capture technology.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Public_transit">
        Public transit
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Research_Triangle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Public transit">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2008-07-05_TTA_bus_713_at_DATA_terminal.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/2008-07-05_TTA_bus_713_at_DATA_terminal.jpg/180px-2008-07-05_TTA_bus_713_at_DATA_terminal.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/2008-07-05_TTA_bus_713_at_DATA_terminal.jpg/270px-2008-07-05_TTA_bus_713_at_DATA_terminal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/2008-07-05_TTA_bus_713_at_DATA_terminal.jpg/360px-2008-07-05_TTA_bus_713_at_DATA_terminal.jpg 2x" width="180"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2008-07-05_TTA_bus_713_at_DATA_terminal.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Triangle Transit bus
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2008-07-11_Chapel_Hill_bus_passing_South_Building.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/2008-07-11_Chapel_Hill_bus_passing_South_Building.jpg/180px-2008-07-11_Chapel_Hill_bus_passing_South_Building.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/2008-07-11_Chapel_Hill_bus_passing_South_Building.jpg/270px-2008-07-11_Chapel_Hill_bus_passing_South_Building.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/2008-07-11_Chapel_Hill_bus_passing_South_Building.jpg/360px-2008-07-11_Chapel_Hill_bus_passing_South_Building.jpg 2x" width="180"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2008-07-11_Chapel_Hill_bus_passing_South_Building.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Chapel Hill Transit bus
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       A partnering system of multiple public transportation agencies currently serves the Triangle region under the joint
       <a href="/wiki/GoTransit_(North_Carolina)" title="GoTransit (North Carolina)">
        GoTransit
       </a>
       branding. Raleigh is served by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Capital_Area_Transit_(Raleigh)" title="Capital Area Transit (Raleigh)">
        Capital Area Transit (CAT)
       </a>
       municipal transit system, while Durham has the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Durham_Area_Transit_Authority" title="Durham Area Transit Authority">
        Durham Area Transit Authority
       </a>
       (DATA) system. Chapel Hill is served by
       <a href="/wiki/Chapel_Hill_Transit" title="Chapel Hill Transit">
        Chapel Hill Transit
       </a>
       , and Cary is served by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C-TRAN_(North_Carolina)" title="C-TRAN (North Carolina)">
        C-Tran
       </a>
       public transit systems. However,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Triangle_Transit" title="Triangle Transit">
        Triangle Transit
       </a>
       , formerly called the Triangle Transit Authority (TTA), works in cooperation with all area transit systems by offering transfers between its own routes and those of the other systems. Triangle Transit also coordinates an extensive
       <a href="/wiki/Vanpool" title="Vanpool">
        vanpool
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Carpool" title="Carpool">
        rideshare
       </a>
       program that serves the region's larger employers and commute destinations.
      </p>
      <p>
       Plans have been made to merge all of the area's municipal systems into Triangle Transit, and Triangle Transit also has proposed a regional rail system to connect downtown Durham, downtown Cary and downtown Raleigh with multiple suburban stops, as well as stops in the Research Triangle Park area. The agency's initial proposal was effectively cancelled in 2006, however, when the agency could not procure adequate federal funding. A committee of local business, transportation and government leaders currently are working with Triangle Transit to develop a new transit blueprint for the region, with various modes of rail transit, as well as
       <a href="/wiki/Bus_rapid_transit" title="Bus rapid transit">
        bus rapid transit
       </a>
       , open as options for consideration.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Air">
        Air
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Research_Triangle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Air">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <h4>
       <span id="Raleigh.E2.80.93Durham_International_Airport_.28RDU.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Raleigh–Durham_International_Airport_(RDU)">
        Raleigh–Durham International Airport (RDU)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Research_Triangle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Raleigh–Durham International Airport (RDU)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Raleigh%E2%80%93Durham_International_Airport" title="Raleigh–Durham International Airport">
        Raleigh–Durham International Airport
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Air_Transport_Association_airport_code" title="International Air Transport Association airport code">
        IATA
       </a>
       :
       <b>
        RDU
       </b>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Civil_Aviation_Organization_airport_code" title="International Civil Aviation Organization airport code">
        ICAO
       </a>
       :
       <b>
        KRDU
       </b>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Federal_Aviation_Administration" title="Federal Aviation Administration">
        FAA
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Location_identifier" title="Location identifier">
        LID
       </a>
       :
       <b>
        RDU
       </b>
       )
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2008-07-30_RDU_welcome_sign.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/2008-07-30_RDU_welcome_sign.jpg/180px-2008-07-30_RDU_welcome_sign.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/2008-07-30_RDU_welcome_sign.jpg/270px-2008-07-30_RDU_welcome_sign.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/2008-07-30_RDU_welcome_sign.jpg/360px-2008-07-30_RDU_welcome_sign.jpg 2x" width="180"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2008-07-30_RDU_welcome_sign.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         RDU welcome sign
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RDU-27527.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1184" data-file-width="1860" height="115" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/RDU-27527.jpg/180px-RDU-27527.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/RDU-27527.jpg/270px-RDU-27527.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/RDU-27527.jpg/360px-RDU-27527.jpg 2x" width="180"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RDU-27527.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         American Airlines
         <a href="/wiki/Boeing_777" title="Boeing 777">
          Boeing 777
         </a>
         touches down at RDU
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2008-07-30_Southwest_Boeing_737_RDU_23R_Final.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/2008-07-30_Southwest_Boeing_737_RDU_23R_Final.jpg/180px-2008-07-30_Southwest_Boeing_737_RDU_23R_Final.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/2008-07-30_Southwest_Boeing_737_RDU_23R_Final.jpg/270px-2008-07-30_Southwest_Boeing_737_RDU_23R_Final.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/2008-07-30_Southwest_Boeing_737_RDU_23R_Final.jpg/360px-2008-07-30_Southwest_Boeing_737_RDU_23R_Final.jpg 2x" width="180"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2008-07-30_Southwest_Boeing_737_RDU_23R_Final.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Southwest Airlines jet landing at RDU
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The General Assembly of North Carolina chartered the Raleigh–Durham Aeronautical Authority in 1939, which was changed in 1945 to the Raleigh–Durham Airport Authority. The first new terminal opened in 1955. Terminal A (now Terminal 1) opened in 1981.
       <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">
        American Airlines
       </a>
       began service to RDU in 1985.
      </p>
      <p>
       RDU opened the 10,000-foot (3,000 m) runway, 5L-23R, in 1986. American Airlines opened its north-south hub operation at RDU in the new Terminal C in June 1987, greatly increasing the size of RDU's operations with a new terminal including a new apron and runway. American brought RDU its first international flights to
       <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">
        Bermuda
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cancun" title="Cancun">
        Cancun
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paris,_France" title="Paris, France">
        Paris
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">
        London
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1996, American Airlines ceased its hub operations at RDU due to
       <a href="/wiki/Pan_American_World_Airways" title="Pan American World Airways">
        Pan Am
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Airlines" title="Eastern Airlines">
        Eastern Airlines
       </a>
       . Pan Am and Eastern were
       <a href="/wiki/Miami_International_Airport" title="Miami International Airport">
        Miami's
       </a>
       main tenants until 1991, when both carriers went bankrupt. Their hubs at MIA were taken over by
       <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">
        United Airlines
       </a>
       and American Airlines. This created a difficulty in competing with
       <a href="/wiki/US_Airways" title="US Airways">
        US Airways
       </a>
       ' hub in
       <a href="/wiki/Charlotte,_North_Carolina" title="Charlotte, North Carolina">
        Charlotte
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">
        Delta Air Lines
       </a>
       ' hub in Atlanta, Georgia for passengers traveling between smaller cities in the North and South.
       <a href="/wiki/Midway_Airlines_(1993%E2%80%932003)" title="Midway Airlines (1993–2003)">
        Midway Airlines
       </a>
       entered the market, starting service in 1995 with the then somewhat novel concept of 50-seat
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canadair_Regional_Jet" title="Canadair Regional Jet">
        Canadair Regional Jets
       </a>
       providing service from its RDU hub primarily along the East Coast. Midway, originally incorporated in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chicago,_Illinois" title="Chicago, Illinois">
        Chicago
       </a>
       , had some success after moving its operations to the midpoint of the eastern United States at RDU and its headquarters to Morrisville, NC. The carrier ultimately could not overcome three weighty challenges: the arrival of
       <a href="/wiki/Southwest_Airlines" title="Southwest Airlines">
        Southwest Airlines
       </a>
       , the refusal of American Airlines to renew the frequent flyer affiliation it had with Midway (thus dispatching numerous higher fare-paying businesspeople to airlines with better reward destinations), and the significant blow of September 11, 2001. Midway Airlines filed
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chapter_11_bankruptcy" title="Chapter 11 bankruptcy">
        Chapter 11 bankruptcy
       </a>
       on August 13, 2001, and ceased operations entirely on October 30, 2003.
      </p>
      <p>
       In February 2000, RDU was ranked as the nation's second fastest-growing major airport in the United States, by Airports Council International, based on 1999 statistics. Passenger growth hit 24% over the previous year, ranking RDU second only to
       <a href="/wiki/Washington_Dulles_International_Airport" title="Washington Dulles International Airport">
        Washington Dulles International Airport
       </a>
       . RDU opened Terminal A south concourse for use by
       <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Airlines" title="Northwest Airlines">
        Northwest
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Continental_Airlines" title="Continental Airlines">
        Continental Airlines
       </a>
       in 2001. The addition added 46,000 square feet (4,300 m
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       ) and five aircraft gates to the terminal. Terminal A became designated as Terminal 1 on October 26, 2008. In 2003, RDU also dedicated a new general aviation terminal. RDU continues to keep pace with its growth by redeveloping Terminal C into a new state-of-the-art terminal, now known as Terminal 2, which opened in October 2008.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Carriers at RDU International Airport:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Air_Canada" title="Air Canada">
         Air Canada
        </a>
        , the airport's first international carrier, introduced service to
        <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">
         Toronto
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">
         Canada
        </a>
        in 1996.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Southwest_Airlines" title="Southwest Airlines">
         Southwest Airlines
        </a>
        , the nation's largest
        <a href="/wiki/Low-cost_carrier" title="Low-cost carrier">
         low-cost carrier
        </a>
        , began service to RDU in 1999.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/America_West" title="America West">
         America West
        </a>
        (merged with
        <a href="/wiki/US_Airways" title="US Airways">
         US Airways
        </a>
        in 2005) began service at RDU in 2002 with flights to
        <a href="/wiki/Phoenix,_Arizona" title="Phoenix, Arizona">
         Phoenix
        </a>
        and
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Las_Vegas,_Nevada" title="Las Vegas, Nevada">
         Las Vegas
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/JetBlue" title="JetBlue">
         JetBlue
        </a>
        began nonstop service between RDU and
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York,_New_York" title="New York, New York">
         New York
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">
         Boston
        </a>
        in 2006, with additional service to
        <a href="/wiki/Fort_Lauderdale,_Florida" title="Fort Lauderdale, Florida">
         Fort Lauderdale
        </a>
        , which began in January 2008.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h4>

      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Private_airfields">
        Private airfields
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Research_Triangle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Private airfields">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>

      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Heliports">
        Heliports
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Research_Triangle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Heliports">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       These licensed
       <a href="/wiki/Heliport" title="Heliport">
        heliports
       </a>
       serve the Research Triangle region:
      </p>

      <p>
       A number of
       <a href="/wiki/Helipad" title="Helipad">
        helipads
       </a>
       (i.e. marked landing sites not classified under the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FAA" title="FAA">
        FAA
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Location_identifier" title="Location identifier">
        LID
       </a>
       system) also serve a variety of additional medical facilities (such as UNC Hospitals in Chapel Hill), as well as private, corporate and governmental interests, throughout the region.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">
        Rail
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Research_Triangle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Rail">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">
        Amtrak
       </a>
       serves the region with the Silver Meteor, Silver Star, Palmetto, Carolinian, and Piedmont routes.

      <p>
       Although still in the planning and evaluation phases as of the end of 2014, the
       <a href="/wiki/Southeast_High_Speed_Rail_Corridor" title="Southeast High Speed Rail Corridor">
        SEHSR
       </a>
       (Southeast High Speed Rail Corridor) project is expected to serve the area.
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Media">
        Media
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Research_Triangle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Media">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The area is part of the Raleigh–Durham–Fayetteville television
       <a href="/wiki/Media_market" title="Media market">
        designated media area
       </a>
       and is the 25th-largest in the country with 1,135,920 households (2014) included in that area and the second largest television market in North Carolina.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is part of the Raleigh–Durham
       <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_Audio" title="Nielsen Audio">
        Nielsen Audio
       </a>
       radio market (code 115) and is the 42nd-largest in the country with a population of 1,365,900.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Raleigh–Durham–Fayetteville market is defined by Nielsen as including Chatham, Cumberland, Dunn, Durham, Granville, Halifax, Harnett, Hoke, Johnston, Lee, Moore, Northampton, Orange, Robeson, Vance, Wake, Warren, Wayne, and Wilson Counties, along with parts of Franklin County.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Print">
        Print
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Research_Triangle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Print">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Numerous newspapers and periodicals serve the Triangle market.
      </p>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Television">
        Television
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Research_Triangle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Television">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Broadcast">
        Broadcast
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Research_Triangle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Broadcast">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       The Triangle is part of the Raleigh–Durham–
       <a href="/wiki/Fayetteville,_North_Carolina" title="Fayetteville, North Carolina">
        Fayetteville
       </a>
       Designated Market Area for broadcast television. As of 2015–16, the area was the 25th-largest in the country. This area includes these television stations:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/UNC-TV" title="UNC-TV">
         WUNC-TV
        </a>
        (4, Chapel Hill), the
        <a href="/wiki/PBS" title="PBS">
         PBS
        </a>
        member station and viewer-supported flagship station of the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_North_Carolina_Television" title="University of North Carolina Television">
         University of North Carolina Television
        </a>
        network
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/WRAL-TV" title="WRAL-TV">
         WRAL-TV
        </a>
        (5, Raleigh), the
        <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">
         NBC
        </a>

      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Cable">
        Cable
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Research_Triangle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Cable">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       Raleigh is home to the Research Triangle Region bureau of the regional
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cable_TV" title="Cable TV">
        cable TV
       </a>
       news channel
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/News_14_Carolina" title="News 14 Carolina">
        News 14 Carolina
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Radio">
        Radio
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Research_Triangle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Radio">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The Triangle is home to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Public_Radio" title="North Carolina Public Radio">
        North Carolina Public Radio
       </a>
       , a public radio station/
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Public_Radio" title="National Public Radio">
        NPR
       </a>
       provider that brings in listeners around the country. Raleigh and a large part of the Triangle area is Arbitron radio market #43. Stations include:
      </p>
